Yarn and Cotton, Double Horse Yarn Becomes Tighter, South China Demand is Particularly Strong, Sales Rebound by 10 Yuan 77

The yarn market has turned from weak to strong. Although the US exchange rate has lengthened and gold has weakened slightly, sentiment has improved. This is because the demand for Chinese yarn is strong in Chaoshan, Guangdong, and other places in South China. As a result, Double Horse yarn is becoming increasingly tight. However, most of the industry believes that the bottom price has reached a high level, so they are unwilling to buy in, and the intention to sell is strong. Therefore, the price fluctuation range is vast, and the competition between the bulls and bears is fierce. The opening price of 20-count Double Horse was 1,016 yuan, and then it rose directly to 1,037 yuan.

News of the morning yarn market opening indicated that the British and American exchange rates had lengthened, the US exchange rate had risen, and gold had fallen, and the selling pressure suddenly increased. The opening price of 20-count Double Horse for April delivery was 1,016 yuan. As soon as this price was opened, the inland merchants bought in as much as possible, and the situation changed immediately. The buying sentiment was strong, and the market rose step by step, closing at 1,037 yuan. Statistics show that the turnover for half a day was 2,637 bales. The spot price of 20-count Double Horse yarn rose by 10 yuan. The amount of purchases by various merchants is listed as follows:

Other merchants: 2,307, Hong Kong: 250

Retrospective of the Woolen Fabric Market Last Year 81

— Mao Fang

(Continued from the 26th)

The current market is frequently rising, but most of the prices have not risen to the cost price. For example, long-haired camel wool is wholesaled at 23 yuan per yard. Those who settled the previous six-month exchange bill at 25% can earn 800 yuan per box. According to the exchange bill settlement, each box will lose 800 yuan per box. The difference in and out of the exchange rate for a box of goods is as high as 1,600 yuan, which shows the relationship between foreign exchange fluctuations and the life of the woolen wool industry. In late autumn, the wool market became more and more brisk, because the weather was cool, and transactions were actively taking place. Both actual sales and the sale of distressed goods were extremely hot. The market on the public tea house changed in an instant, with prices jumping three or four times a day. Because the European war had broken out, the supply was limited, and it was expected that it would be difficult to obtain a fixed supply in the future, so all those with inventory on hand were hoarding and arbitrarily raising prices. The general delivery merchants all held the door market's sample business, no longer calling for the street to solicit business, and the business of brokers, except for those with financial resources and courage, eating goods themselves and using the means of control, could make a lot of money, were all more difficult than in previous years.

The market was even better in October, because the weather was getting colder and the sales of various men's suits were extremely wide. The shop door merchants of woolen fabric clothing stores in this street, both old and new, shoe markets, and hat factories all had smooth sales. However, customer merchants (1) had transportation difficulties, and (2) most of the wool weaving materials were designated as luxury goods by the government, so there were very few who transported and sold them to the mainland. However, the procurement of guerrilla areas such as Tianjin, Hankou, and Nanjing was extremely active. At the end of the month, the price of the border goods was even higher than at the beginning of the month. Various thick and thin woolen fabrics, whether woven from wool, cotton, silk, or ramie, imported goods or local factory goods woven in Shanghai, all rose steadily, like flying a kite, higher and higher. The main reasons are: first, the shortening of exchange bills increased costs and raw materials rose sharply, and various prices rose sharply and expenses were huge; second, the European war was difficult to fix and the market sales were smooth, and the recent price increase of 2 cents, the customs duty was forced to use "Hua Xing" banknotes, which invisibly increased by 40%. Woolen fabrics with Western characters are still popular and sell well. Western clothing stores on Xiafei Road, Sichuan Road, Daxin Street, and Jing'an Temple mostly display them in the glass windows of the front door as a sign of honor. Cabbage green and light green patterned fabrics are still very popular and show off, and demand exceeds supply. Overcoat fabrics have shifted to light gray as the trend. In mid-winter, due to difficulty in fixing deliveries, and the lack of Shanghai inventory, all goods are in short supply. Sellers with inventory, whether retail or wholesale, are all hoarding and arbitrarily raising prices. General wholesalers are overjoyed. The prices of domestic woolen fabrics and serge have risen sharply, because the raw materials are scarce and difficult to transport. The price increase of overcoat fabrics and thick fabrics is also not light. Camel wool scarves (also known as cloth covers) are more popular than riding breeches. The prices of all colors are the same, unlike last year, when the price difference between colors was as high as one yuan. Woolen fabrics that were previously loaded on German ships and stranded in Japan have now been transported one after another by ships from neutral countries, and the number is not small. Woolen fabrics arriving in Shanghai have decreased by two-thirds compared with before, because the Japanese government ordered that woolen fabrics must be mixed with artificial wool and cotton, resulting in a sharp reduction in demand, and also because of foreign exchange purchases, they cannot be directly shipped to Shanghai without first being transferred to Hong Kong. Shanghai-made woven woolen fabrics have been greatly sold as a result of good opportunities. Japanese businessmen operating in the business also have the Jia Gong Da Yarn Factory weaving woolen fabrics, and Chinese businessmen also have Run Feng, Da Hua, and De Da, etc. Those who specialize in linings, such as Zi cloth, have Yin Feng, Xin Ji, Zheng Lun, and Bao Kang, etc., which can also be seen as flourishing. The market in the last quarter of the year has always risen without falling, because the shortage of goods is abnormal, and the industry is very optimistic. Also, because the scheduled deliveries are completely absent, many have purchased spring and summer spot goods, so the spring and winter woolen fabric deliveries have a great business. But in fact, all goods are in short supply, and prices are high. At the public tea house, only the sound of wanting to buy in is heard, and rarely is the sound of wanting to sell out heard. The samples produced by the distributors have been raised one after another on a temporary basis, and most of them have been recalled early, which can also be seen as the lack of precious woolen fabrics. The standard is chaotic, 70-80% of it is controlled by large wholesalers, and the market is high, allowing those who hoard goods to shout wildly. All transactions are mostly settled by the buyer following the seller. Looking at the market conditions in the four seasons, the prices have risen every day, especially in the winter. The profits of all sizes of shops are all more than those in 1927. (End)

The Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Kuomintang issued a letter to the public, saying: Compatriots, we should understand that the Japanese invasion of China is approaching total collapse. There is no way to pull out the muddy feet in military affairs. When the mountains and rivers are exhausted, they have to launch a political offensive again, instigating pseudo-organizations, using Wang Kemin, Liang Hongzhi, and even Wang Jingwei, in an attempt to save their final fate. In fact, this strategy still cannot affect our national policy of resistance and reconstruction in the slightest. Now our front-line battles are reporting victories frequently. We firmly believe that our leader has clearly told us that the final victory is 100% sure to come soon. Military experts around the world have also confirmed that the final victory will belong to China. The Japanese domestic situation is in extreme panic. Only those who are blinded by greed and suffering from a very heavy fear of Japan, cannot see the dawn of victory, and still sell themselves to rely on, which has to be said to be a great shame for the Chinese nation. We must wash away this shame. We must strive for the independence and freedom of the Chinese nation. We must exert the power of 450 million citizens. Two Concessions Under Special Curfew Starting This Morning 83

Starting at zero o'clock this morning, the authorities of the two concessions declared a special curfew. At the intersection of Rue Eduard VII and Avenue Foch, which is the boundary between the Public Concession and the French Concession, following past practices, all unimportant roads running north-south will be blocked with wire mesh, cutting off traffic. Only the Bund, Sichuan Road, Sam Ye Ge Bridge, Zheng Jia Mu Bridge, Dong Xin Bridge, Great World, Chengdu Road, Tong Fu Road and other intersections can pass north and south. The number of guards has been increased, and pedestrians and vehicles are strictly checked. The border areas between the two concessions and the outer areas are also stepping up defenses. Police personnel from the two concessions and troops stationed in various countries have been dispatched to maintain order.

British Troops in Xinjiang Road Defense Zone Raise Iron Netting Higher, Citizens Outside the Boundary Near North Xizang Road Are Uneasy 84

Since the Xin Zha Branch of the Zhabei Branch (formerly the Fourth District) was hit by the troops, all the municipal housing, except for the section from the north side of the Xin Zha Bridge, Guangfu Road, and Chang'an Road facing west, to the Huasheng Road intersection, still has dozens of low-rise tile bungalows. The hundreds of houses in Xinjiang Road De Xing Lane, Tian Xin Lane, Tian Bao Lane, Sheng Chang Lane, Nan Lin Lane, Hua Xing Road, Hua Xing Fang, etc., are inhabited by poor citizens. Because the rents and prices in the concessions are too expensive, they have all moved back one after another in recent times, but they spend every day in painful conditions. However, the roads there are adjacent to the concessions and are British troop defense zones. In recent days, there have been more than a dozen British soldiers (i.e. Scottish soldiers) who have thickened the original barbed wire and raised it by five or six feet. Yesterday morning, even though there were continuous rain, the work did not stop. It has now been added from the intersection of Hainin Road and Gansu Road to Rehe Road, nearly to the intersection of North Xizang Road.

All Sectors Lowered Flags Yesterday to Commemorate Revolutionary Martyrs, Inheriting Their Will, Emulating Revolutionary Spirit, Supporting National Policy, and Completing the Great Cause of Resistance and National Reconstruction 85

Yesterday was the anniversary of the martyrdom of the 72 martyrs of Huanghuagang, also known as Revolutionary Martyrs' Memorial Day. The Central Government also stipulated that the commemoration of the martyrdom of Deng Zhongxia, Chen Ying Shi, Liao Zhongkai, and Zhu Zhixin, as well as the death anniversaries of Huang Keqiang and Hu Zhangtang, should be held together. All sectors of the city lowered their flags and suspended entertainment banquets in solemn remembrance, in order to express their admiration for the heroic sacrifices and great achievements of the martyrs. Schools, public organizations, courts, the Jianghai Customs, and other institutions all took holidays as usual. All sectors recognized that the true meaning of commemorating the revolutionary martyrs lay in emulating their revolutionary spirit and inheriting their unfinished aspirations. Therefore, they unanimously and resolutely supported the national policy and completed the resistance and national reconstruction, in order to carry forward the foundation left by the martyrs. All sectors continued to promote the austerity and relief movement to benefit the refugees. The authorities of the two concessions implemented strict security measures yesterday, increasing the number of plainclothes and uniformed police patrols. Any suspicious pedestrians and vehicles were inspected to prevent bad elements from disrupting public order.

Japanese Side Plots Again to Interfere with Cotton Yarn Procurement and Sales, Unification Policy Repeatedly Fails, Headed Down Wrong Path Without Realization 86

After the Japanese side unified various goods and monopolized the market in the occupied areas and the suburbs of Shanghai, they are currently implementing the following: the "Fuli Company" unified the tea in Dinghai, the "Central China Company" unified the silk and silkworms in the occupied areas, and the recently opened "Central Market" unified the vegetables from the suburbs to Shanghai. All of them have failed. Now the Japanese side has an organization called the "Textile Co., Ltd." in the works, hoping to once again unify the purchase and sale of cotton yarn from Chinese-owned yarn mills. It is said that this organization is in the works and will be formally established in the middle of next month. Before the war, there were about 40 Chinese-owned yarn mills operating in Shanghai. Some of the factories were destroyed by artillery fire during the war because they were located in Zhabei and Yangshupu. Since the National Government worked hard to develop the southwest and northwest, the factories operated by Chinese have gradually moved to the mainland to continue production in order to meet needs and consolidate the financial foundation during the war. Therefore, there are currently about 20 Chinese-owned yarn mills that have resumed operations in Shanghai. In peacetime, Nantong was the largest supplier of raw cotton, supplemented by products from Zhengzhou, Shaanxi, and other places. The cotton from Tongzhou is soft and has long fibers, comparable to American cotton. It is suitable for spinning finer counts of yarn. Orders from abroad are mostly for American, Indian, and Egyptian cotton. Since the outbreak of the War of Resistance, the raw materials shipped to China from the occupied and unoccupied areas have been difficult after the outbreak of the war, but they can still come in without being unified. The power to import foreign cotton to Shanghai is controlled by foreign merchants, which is beyond the power of the Japanese side.

General Mutō can rest, why so much tongue-wagging?

Shanghai Municipal Council Urges Citizens to Prevent Infectious Diseases 90

The Public Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council announces that, as spring arrives and infectious diseases tend to spread, the following four public health regulations are hereby enacted to protect the health of the public and residents within the Settlement. Please take note: (1) Vaccinations and cholera inoculations are free. Vaccinations and inoculations are available at all health sub-stations and in mobile vaccination vehicles. (2) If there are any unsanitary conditions in your residence, please report them to the nearest health sub-station. Inspectors will be sent to help. (3) Houses that have been affected by infectious diseases can be disinfected free of charge by the nearest health sub-station. The Isolation Hospital at 96 Haining Road provides free care for people with dangerous infectious diseases. However, there will be a charge for special rooms and medications.

From April 1st to October 30th, stalls must close before 10:00 AM daily so that cleaners can clear away garbage early. An announcement has already been issued.

French Concession Price Stabilization Committee Diligently Investigating, Drafting Detailed Price Control Regulations, and Enforcing Them Strictly, Committee Members Wasting No Time 92

The English-language *North China Daily News* reports that the promulgation of price control regulations by the French Concession's Price Stabilization Committee has been delayed for some time. When a reporter inquired with French Consul-General Eugene, he replied that no committee member was wasting time. The entire matter was very complex, and the committee was working closely with the Shanghai Municipal Council subcommittee. Although the work was slow, it needed to be effective. Price control regulations were still being drafted and would be strictly enforced as soon as they were finalized. The Price Stabilization Committee had held many meetings to discuss these regulations. It was necessary to understand the economic situation in Shanghai before deciding on price control regulations. Any steps we take must be practical and necessary. We do not want to implement regulations that require subsequent amendment. To achieve this goal, the Price Stabilization Committee is proceeding cautiously and discussing everything with the Shanghai Municipal Council subcommittee, which takes time. Although it may seem delayed on the surface, it is not because the Price Stabilization Committee is not working. It is simply because a great deal of time has been spent on this work. No Progress in Fact After Establishment of Police Agreement, Special Police Force Still Far from Being Established, No Sign of Returning Hongkou Police Authority 93

Regarding the issue of road extensions outside the boundary of the Shanghai Western District, the Shanghai Municipal Council signed a temporary police agreement with the so-called "Municipal Government" on February 16, deciding to establish a jointly operated special police force on the extended roads. Regarding the issue of returning police authority in Hongkou, the Shanghai Municipal Council signed the Suzhou Creek North District police agreement with Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai Miura Yoshiaki on March 1, deciding to establish a new "E" District police district in Hongkou. At the same time, the Japanese side would return all police authority in the Hongkou and Yangshupu areas to the Shanghai Municipal Council. To date, there has been no progress in fact. The special police force in the Shanghai Western District has not been established, and the Shanghai Municipal Council has not yet resumed full police authority in the Hongkou and Yangshupu areas.

When a reporter inquired with Police Commissioner Major F.W. Gerrard yesterday, it was learned that no committee meeting had been held to discuss the establishment of the "E" District police district, and even the committee members had not been appointed. The Police Department's resumption of full authority to exercise its functions north of Suzhou Creek would not occur until after the "E" District police district was established. At the same time, the conference on preparations for the new police force on the extended roads outside the boundary of the Shanghai Western District had been delayed for a long time and was still far from being established. In that area, bandits were rampant, and cases of robbery and theft were constantly occurring, which urgently needed to be addressed. According to yesterday's Shanghai Municipal Council Gazette, a section regarding the future of the area north of Suzhou Creek stated that, on December 10, 1938, Mr. Hidaka wrote to the Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council stating that the Japanese authorities would continue to lift restrictions in that area as much as possible. The Council sincerely hoped that the attitude expressed in his communication would be reciprocated and that all restrictions would be lifted as soon as possible.

Coal Inventory Growing Daily 94

370,000 Tons Shipped to Shanghai in Two Months, Valued at Over 7 Million National Currency

Anthracite coal is continuously shipped into Shanghai from Japan, and inventories are growing daily. Transactions are also being concluded via telegram, so the spot market supply is increasing. Major dealers are releasing coal to the market, but prices have not fallen. It is assured that there will be no shortage of coal and fuel in Shanghai. The authorities have already formulated concrete measures to urge coal merchants to sell coal at fair prices so that speculators cannot manipulate the market and prices will fall. From January to February this year, a total of 376,129 tons of coal were shipped from overseas, valued at 7,264,043 national currency. In February, 174,277 tons were shipped, valued at 3,817,647 national currency (1,410,287 in gold). The largest amount came from Annam, totaling 104,779 tons, valued at 787,300 in gold. British India was second, totaling 43,928 tons, valued at 531,839 in gold. Japan was third, totaling 13,289 tons, valued at 49,818 in gold. However, Japanese coal is of lower quality, so customers are extremely rare. There is no concern that the supply of firewood and charcoal fuel will be interrupted. If the direct shipping of Ningbo freighters is realized, a large amount of Wenzhou and Taizhou firewood and charcoal will be shipped, and the price of firewood and charcoal will plummet at that time.

Japanese Planes Disrupt and Tragically Bomb Shangyu 96

Eastern Zhejiang, which had been quiet for some time, has once again become active with Japanese planes. At 9:30 AM on the 27th of this month, three Japanese planes were spotted in Baiguan, Shaoxing, dropping three bombs on nearby mountains, injuring three civilians. At 9:00 AM on the same day, five Japanese planes were spotted in Shangyu County, dropping thirteen bombs, including two incendiary bombs. The county party headquarters, post office, and Nanda Street caught fire. According to a reporter from the New Voice News Agency, the Shanghai World Red Swastika Society received a telegram from the Shangyu Red Swastika Society yesterday, stating that on the 27th, Baiguan, Xiaoyue, and Wucheyan were bombed. Our relief team rushed to provide assistance and returned to the Society this morning. At 9:00 AM, the county seat was bombed, causing a raging fire. There were over 500 deaths and injuries and thousands of houses destroyed. The disaster was tragic. A telegram was sent to request relief. Shangyu Red Swastika Society (28th).

Dredging of Huangpu Silt Expected to Begin 97

The dredging of the Huangpu River was halted after the Shanghai Incident and has been suspended for nearly three years. Silt near Jiaozui Island (Dinghai Island) has gradually accumulated, affecting navigation. Ships are anchored outside the Huangpu River, and both sides of the streets in the settlements are flooded during every rain. It is learned that the dredging work will be started by a small dredger within two weeks. China's largest dredger, the "Jianshe," is unlikely to participate in this work. It will undertake the dredging work when the weather is dry. Another dredger, a sister ship of the "Jianshe," is currently stranded in Danze. It is learned that it will not be transported to Shanghai until after the end of the European war.

American Consul General Gauss has formally notified the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement that, effective the 26th of this month, he will transfer consular affairs to Consul Peck. The foreign press corps in Shanghai held a banquet at the American Club yesterday to bid farewell to Mr. Gauss. In addition to Mr. Gauss, those who attended the banquet included Mr. Peck, the administrative consul of the American Consulate, who will serve as acting Consul General after Mr. Gauss leaves Shanghai, as well as Mr. Abend, reporter for the New York Times, Mr. Pyle, reporter for United Press, Mr. Ford, reporter for the North China Daily News, and Mr. Harris, reporter for Associated Press.

British First Lord of the Admiralty Churchill to Broadcast to Shanghai 99

Can Be Heard Sunday Morning

British First Lord of the Admiralty Churchill is scheduled to broadcast to the Far East from the British Broadcasting Corporation at 8:20 PM to 8:35 PM tonight. The Shanghai listening time will be 3:20 AM to 3:35 AM on Sunday (the 31st). The broadcast will be relayed directly from London on longwave. The broadcast on Sunday (today) will be broadcast in three locations. The first broadcast in Shanghai time will be at 8:30 AM, relayed by transmitter number 5. The second broadcast will be at 2:15 PM Shanghai time, relayed by transmitter number 1 with call signs GSA, GSW, and GRX. The final broadcast will be at 9:30 PM Shanghai time, relayed by transmitter number 3 with call signs GSA, GSW, and GSE. Shanghai listeners should be able to receive the broadcast at the specified times. This is the second time British First Lord of the Admiralty has broadcast to the Far East since the European War.

The Board of Directors recently resolved to add a surcharge of 50% to the general rate, land tax, special house rate, and special advertising tax from July 1st of last year. The above revenue estimates are based on relevant facts. If there are no unexpected changes during the year, they should be achieved. The tax collection measures implemented in the eastern district last winter were successful and will be continued this year.

(1) Shanghai Power Company 3,650,000 yuan, (2) West Shanghai Electricity Company 765,000 yuan, (3) China General Omnibus Company 185,000 yuan, (4) Shanghai Electric Construction Company 300,000 yuan, (5) Shanghai Waterworks Company 165,000 yuan, (6) French Tramway Company 10,500 yuan, (7) Shanghai Telephone Company 260,000 yuan.

(C) Current Expenditure

The drastic decline in exchange rates and the sharp rise in prices of various goods and materials have had a significant impact, especially on the payment of retirement savings and pensions in the general expenditure category. Due to the high cost of living, Council employees must be given higher allowances to show consideration. In addition, the salaries of employees who should be promoted according to their grade will also be increased accordingly. However, Western employees whose home countries are involved in the European war will not be granted long leave this year, which will save a considerable amount on long leave exchange allowances and travel expenses.

Interest and commissions, etc. This expenditure includes the interest payable on municipal bonds and temporary loans, totaling 2,987,360 yuan this year, an increase of 753,780 yuan over last year.

Repayment of 6% New Bonds. It is planned to issue 12 million yuan in new bonds this year, with a term of ten years. Principal will be repaid every six months starting from July next year. General Expenditure. This type of expenditure is divided into the following four items, totaling 8,000,570 yuan this year, an increase of 5,304,920 yuan over last year.

Suzhou Road Fire the Previous Night - Losses Reaching One Million Yuan - Firefighters Bravely Fighting the Blaze - Walls Collapsing with Terrifying Sounds 108

The Continental Daily reports: At 9:30 PM on the 27th, a fire suddenly broke out at warehouse number 796 on Suzhou Road. It contained a large quantity of raw cotton and silk cocoons, some of which were already destroyed. It was previously reported that the warehouse belonged to Jardine Matheson, but according to Jardine Matheson's statement, the warehouse is the property of the Bank of China and leased to Jardine Matheson. The goods stored inside all belong to various Chinese merchants. As of yesterday (the 28th) evening, some parts of the warehouse were still burning. It is estimated that these remaining embers, blocked by rubble and inaccessible to water, will

continue to burn for several days

before being extinguished. Yesterday, firefighters were still on-site, drawing water to pour onto the smoldering silk, wood, and raw cotton beneath the rubble, and knocking down dangerous walls. The upper floors and roof of the warehouse were completely destroyed, and the rear wall was

damaged. Total losses are estimated at six hundred thousand to one million yuan, but the exact value of the lost goods will not be known for several

months. It is reported that most of the goods stored on the second floor of the warehouse were salvaged and undamaged, while

the ground floor only suffered water damage.

The owners of the goods will soon prepare a list of their goods for investigation. According to the Fire Department, firefighters arrived at the scene shortly after 9:30 PM on the 27th. Due to the burning cotton and billowing thick smoke, firefighters wearing gas masks rushed into the building to pour water on the heart of the fire. Several fire trucks were parked behind the warehouse. The commander, seeing the rear wall swaying dangerously, urgently ordered the trucks to move away and the firefighters inside to evacuate. But before the firefighters could leave the building, the rear wall

collapsed,

the sound of it crashing was terrifying.

Fortunately, no one nearby was crushed under the wall. Shortly after all the firefighters had exited the building, the first floor immediately collapsed. Subsequently, water was poured inside through the windows. By 2:30 AM, the fire had passed the critical point, and a few firefighters were left on site to monitor and continue to pour water on the unextinguished areas, up to this moment.

Late that night, as these three couples of different nationalities were about to leave after gambling, they suddenly encountered a group of drunk men of a certain nationality who forcibly grabbed the hands of their wives, attempting indecent assault. The Dutch man, seeing this, became enraged, but faced with being outnumbered, he ran to the nearby fake "police station." There, an "officer" who could speak English repeatedly thanked him, but said he could not help. The Dutch man, helpless, ran back to the Huile Palace, where the three couples found themselves surrounded by an officer and his thirty or so Chinese assistants, who were very aggressive. In self-defense, the Dutch man took the initiative and struck down a Japanese man with his cane, and thus the fight formally began. A person of a certain nationality immediately took out a pistol and fired, but the Dutch man, quick-witted, knocked the pistol out of his hand with his cane. The brawl lasted for an hour and a half before ending. According to eyewitnesses, the three wives fought bravely during the brawl, and there were no seriously fatal injuries.

suddenly heard the explosion and were quite alarmed, thinking it was a bomb and scrambling to take cover. The ships in the Huangpu River then sounded

their sirens, and the Puji fireboat immediately sailed to the burning boat to pour water on it. British and Chinese gunboats in the Huangpu River also turned on searchlights to assist. Old News Newly Copied - Sixty-Seven Years Ago (339) 116

(From this newspaper in the twelfth year of the Tongzhi reign of the late Qing Dynasty)

Officials (2)

How can it be said that people scheme for themselves? When a mediocre ruler is in power, the ministers seize control. The mediocre ruler gives the great authority to his subjects and it's misused, and the ministers sell official positions for their own gain. Even if they don't sell them, many are given ranks in public court, and thanks are given in private chambers, so the subjects are all planting parties and marketing favors. For example, Liu Xin and Yang Xiong of the Western Han Dynasty were talented people, but they were willing to be followers of Wang Mang, disgracing their names after death. Cui Lie of the Eastern Han Dynasty paid 100,000 cash to become Minister of Works, and people called him "the copper-smelling Minister". As for other generals and colonels, there's no need to mention them. During the Five Dynasties period, there were many people who knew how to seek wealth and forget their families. Later, there were even those who recognized people as their fathers and offered the Sixteen Prefectures of Yanyun to seek appointment as emperor. It is even less worth mentioning that petty people buy and sell official positions. Furthermore, with the addition of Wu Sansi, Tian Lingzi, Qin Hui, and Jia Sidao, almost all court officials came from their factions. How could the Tang and Song dynasties not perish! It is difficult to describe the disorder of the Yuan Dynasty in words. At the beginning of the Ming Dynasty, the politics were still admirable, but Wang Zhen's interference opened the way for eunuchs to seize power. By the time of the Tianqi Emperor, Wei Zhongxian had half of the court officials as his adopted sons, and bandits rose up everywhere, making the Ming Dynasty beyond salvation. Moreover, Emperor Zhuanglie inherited the throne with stubbornness, how could the Ming Dynasty's society not collapse. Official positions are originally established by the court to await virtuous talents and to govern the people, but how can they be allowed to be bought and sold by the subjects? By the time they are all bought and sold, the affairs of the time are beyond hope. It is difficult to investigate matters of the distant past, but the events of the Ming Dynasty are still before us. It is said that Wei Zhongxian's adopted sons paid silver to get positions, and those who still had a conscience were afraid of being known, while those who had lost their conscience were afraid of not being known, so they had their parties publicize it, showing off their ability to manipulate things. With the affairs of the Ming Dynasty like this, what were they waiting for to perish!

Free Talk

Thoughts

Seeds of Evolution 117

— Yang Tongfang

The meaning and value of an individual's life are entirely based on the extent of their understanding of thought. In psychology, thought occupies the highest level of all conscious activity, being a systematic union of correct ideas. Humans possess the most complete nervous system, thus transcending ordinary higher animals. In order to achieve the goal of perpetual survival and continuous development, one cannot but utilize thought to control the natural and social environment.

To enhance the meaning of life and solve the many difficulties that arise in daily life, we must train our minds to achieve our goals. As Professor Thorndike said, "The creation of human material culture and the progress of scientific research all depend on mental activity." Any living creature other than humans is subject to the natural environment to maintain its survival, while humans alone can control nature to improve the social environment and obtain all the necessities of life. Is this not all because humans have the power of thought?

Therefore, if humans want to control the social environment, create a high level of spiritual culture, and achieve the goals of survival and evolution, they must rely on the development of their minds. Whether human life evolves or not can be seen from the progress and decline of thought. Promoting the development of human thought still depends on the capacity to study and control nature. In the last four hundred years or so, thought in Europe has been particularly developed, which is why science has made such amazing progress. If it were not for Copernicus and Galileo loudly advocating methods of thought, could there have been such achievements? The development of human culture and the improvement of life depend on the progress of thought; the progress of thought depends on the development of scientific knowledge, which is undoubtedly true.

Thought originates from doubt, and doubt originates from difficulties in life. We do not develop any thoughts when everything goes smoothly in what we do; conversely, when our methods of dealing with life are no longer adapted to actual situations, that is, when difficulties are unresolved, thought arises. Difficulty is the sole condition for the generation of thought, and the progress of the human material environment depends entirely on whether we are satisfied with life. We should constantly study, control, and improve our own environment and find more problems in life to give appropriate solutions in order to train correct thinking. Why is the thinking of scientists particularly developed? There is no other reason except that they can pay attention to things that others do not notice, and they can often raise doubts and seek problems. Newton noticed the apple falling to the ground, thus inventing the law of gravity. Galileo's invention of the pendulum was due to his noticing the swinging lamp in the church. To see what is suspicious and not question it, to avoid difficulties, will never generate thought, advance culture, or enlighten human intelligence.

If we want to raise our ideals of life, we can only break the inertia of thought from time to time. We should be serious about our attitude towards life. When we encounter difficulties, we must find appropriate solutions, and we must pay attention to the subtle things in daily life and grasp the opportunities that trigger thought—within them lies the seed of human evolution!

— Yibei

Cultivation

The Necessary Conditions for Being a Leader 119

— Xu Meng

If a person is to succeed as a leader in business, in a group, or in other similar groups, then the following conditions are necessary:

(A) Personality Aspects

(1) Have a clear purpose and goals.

(2) Have courage, enthusiasm, activity, and ambition.

(3) Have a unique personality and prestige; be able to command respect and even more so, be able to inspire unwavering trust.

(4) Have unique insights beyond ordinary people, and even more so, have a firm sense of self-confidence, and never abandon yourself to despair.

(5) Have a sound mind and a fair and noble character.

(6) Have a cheerful and peaceful temperament; without impatience or arrogance.

(7) Have a sense of humor in conversation.

(B) Handling Affairs

(1) Have a broad vision, be able to plan, and have the ability to organize groups.

(2) When faced with any difficult task, one should not avoid difficulties but bravely tackle it.

(3) Be firm and patient in doing things, never give up halfway, and should be consistent from beginning to end.

(4) Be able to make decisive decisions and even more so, be able to adapt to changing circumstances.

(5) Have a shrewd and skilled approach to the things that should be done in business.

(6) Be capable and intelligent, and also have imagination and creative talent.

(C) Cultivation for Dealing with the World

A. How to treat people?

(1) When people have shortcomings, patiently persuade, guide, and encourage them; be able to make them strive to achieve and even more so, be able to arouse others' self-confidence.

(2) Accept others' criticisms and opinions with a sincere attitude.

(3) As for social interaction, one should have flexible skills and a quick tongue.

(4) Treat others with sincerity and without deception.

B. How to treat subordinates?

(1) Have deep concern and sympathy for one's own subordinates.

(2) Praise and value the merits and creations of subordinates.

(3) Be able to recognize people and even more so, be able to use people.

(4) Those who perform well should be praised and rewarded; the condemnation of those who perform poorly should be appropriate and effective, and one should never lose one's temper indiscriminately.

(D) Other

(1) Have a clear understanding of the current situation.

(2) Have the ability to control the environment in which one is situated.

Profession

Another Side of the Career Circle 120

— Quying

Reading Mr. Yingjin's "In the Career Circle" evokes endless feelings. In today's era of arduous nation-building, tens of thousands of young people enter the so-called "career circle" in groups for economic reasons, carrying full enthusiasm and hope, only to be rewarded with hypocrisy and snobbery. Millions of young people on the isolated island are wandering around in anxiety! How can their pure and enthusiastic minds withstand such illegal devastation?

Since my hometown was occupied by special forces, I have been wandering on the isolated island for three years. It was difficult to get a job. Holding a golden rice bowl, I never did things carelessly. After a month, I began to realize that the difficulty of the job was not in the work, but in dealing with people.

In most commercial firms, there are factions among the internal staff. They consider themselves to belong to a certain faction. Among them, there seems to be a tight organization, whose only responsibility is to attack other factions; to stir up trouble out of nothing and to suck up to superiors -- commonly known as "licking boots". Their skills of concealing evil and promoting good (?!) are indeed worthy of admiration, always with a smiling face, and never saying anything bad in front of people. Shortly after I stepped in there, a social worker from a certain faction tried to pull me into the faction. Because I didn't understand the internal situation, I firmly refused.

Then merciless fate rushed upon me!

A week later, I was invited (?) by the manager into the solemn court. He instructed me that I must consult the advanced people in everything, especially Mr. So-and-so, the social worker, who was the most capable, and finally said, "You are still in the probation period." I had to say yes.

On the way back, I thought to myself that there was no fault in my duties, but I encountered such difficulties. For the sake of the burden on my family, I could not resolutely resign. I began to plan how to deal with it.

I changed my policy and often chatted with them during rest time. For the sake of self-esteem, of course, I did not engage in flattery. Soon, their discrimination against me gradually decreased.

When I looked around at those sharp, wolf-like eyes, I always responded with a sincere smile. I always completed their instructions quickly. Perhaps they were moved! The big knife hidden in the smiling face seemed to have shortened a lot.

As for their false accusations, they were skilled at attacking others. I stood firm, and I never did anything carelessly in my duties, and finally made them unable to use their skills. Now they no longer attack me -- another colleague told me. Although I did not join their group, I was always living in endurance. Soon, the manager summoned me to the office again and encouraged me to work hard, as if I was doing a good job.

Looking back on my own experience, although I feel chilled, there are often dark prospects in a happy environment; conversely. How can there be no dawn in a dark life?

Young friends, work hard!

(Moved to help those in need)

Teachers Like Rice 121

— Old Elephant

Teachers are like "meals." Tolerant teachers are like white rice, and strict teachers are like brown rice. White rice tastes good, but it is not as nutritious as brown rice. Students often like to eat white rice.

If the teacher is shoddy, the student will develop malnutrition. Now there are more white rice teachers than brown rice teachers on the isolated island, so there are too many malnourished students.

Malnutrition is very dangerous, and if it is not quickly adjusted, it will be difficult to cure in the future. They sigh that their fate is not as good as that of the weevils who eat rice. Qu Fu writes

A Word on the Cross (Continued) 122

The words that Jesus prayed to the Heavenly Father included many people; those who ridiculed him on the spot, the Roman officials, the Roman soldiers, the Jewish priests, etc. were all included, "Father, forgive them." This not only showed his trust in God, and his love for his enemies, but also implied the parent-child relationship between the world and God. When a child wants something from his father, he also calls out again and again, "Father, Father." Is it not strange that Jesus asked for mercy and forgiveness for sinners? God was on Mount Sinai, with thunder in front and hail behind, protecting him, the mountains collapsed and the earth cracked, how great, how solemn. But on the cross of Calvary, injured, thirsty, on the verge of death, he still cried out loudly, "Father, forgive them, for they know not what they do." A religion with power is great, but a religion with love is even greater, a just religion is great, but a religion that seeks mercy for others is even greater. Legend has it that a soldier committed a crime and was about to be taken to the officer for trial. He was a person who often committed crimes and had often been punished. As soon as the officer mentioned his name, he said, "Has this man committed a crime again? He has been given all the ways to reform." At that time, a subordinate officer came forward and said, "I am telling my superior that there is only one thing that has not been done for him." "What?" "He has never been forgiven." The officer was a little surprised when he heard this, and said, "Forgive him?" "He thought for a while and ordered someone to bring the prisoner in and ask him what he wanted to say." The soldier replied, "No, I just feel pain for what I have done." At this time, there was an expression on his face, as if he had no hope other than being severely punished for his crime. The officer looked at him with great compassion and said, "Well, we have given you all kinds of ways to reform, now I will forgive you once to see the effect." The soldier was so moved that tears streamed down his face. It is said that from that day on, he became a new person, and became a decent person in society, no longer wearing soldier's clothes. Therefore, I say that a religion with power is great, but a religion with love is even greater.

If you want to ask in detail and research, please write to mailbox 1227.

Entertainment World

Exceptional Artist: Walt Disney 123

— Hua Ji

Ever since Walt Disney achieved great success with "Snow White," he has continued to work diligently and strive for perfection. His latest work, "Pinocchio," has already arrived in Shanghai, and its content has been previously introduced in this newspaper. Now, let's talk about this great artist's everyday interactions with people.

Over a Hundred Assistants

Under Walt Disney's direction, there are also five directors, thirty-one assistants, fifty-six deputy assistants, thirty-two renowned painters specializing in characters, actions, and expressions, and twenty-six painters specializing in backgrounds. There are also twenty-one effects assistants… In total, he has over a hundred assistants, and they are all top-notch cartoonists and artists in America… The reason he can get so many people to work for him willingly is fourfold:

Understanding Colleagues

The first reason, of course, is that he is willing to give people very generous compensation. This can be done by anyone with large capital.

Second: Disney is a very understanding person. If someone is hindered by their work due to a headache or illness, he always asks them to go back and rest. Although on the surface, the loss of one person's work is inevitable, he knows that the results of forcing someone to work are never good.

Not Ashamed to Ask Those Below

Third: He has the virtue of "not being ashamed to ask those below." Although he is the most famous cartoonist in the world, he has no arrogant habits. Once, he saw someone shaking their head at his original manuscript. He sincerely asked for their criticism. The person mustered their courage and pointed out his mistakes. Disney immediately smiled and accepted their opinion and solemnly treated them to a meal.

True Skill

Fourth: He truly has real skills. One day, an employee of Walt Disney walked into his office and saw Disney buried in his work. Upon seeing it, he admired him to the point of prostration because Disney had completed sixteen paintings in a very short time. If he were asked to do it, it would take him a whole day! Therefore, his employees all admire him, respect him, and wholeheartedly cooperate with him. An artist like this is naturally worthy of our emulation.

Movie Novel

Prelude to "The Fragrant Concubine" 124

— Zhao Nv

Emperor Gaozong (Qianlong) of the Qing Dynasty was fond of grand achievements and used troops in all directions. After pacifying the Jungar Khanate, he ordered General Zhao Hui to conquer Xinjiang. The rulers of Xinjiang, the brothers Burhanuddin and Khoja Jihan, Khoja had a wife named Fragrant Concubine, who was beautiful and virtuous and had a unique fragrance, hence her name. At that time, the Qing army was approaching Xinjiang's borders. The Fragrant Concubine was hunting with other women, and the citizens bowed to her on the road, vying to ask about national affairs. The concubine said that a battle might be unavoidable. The citizens, hearing this, were filled with righteous indignation and were willing to die for their country. An old melon seller, though old, was full of vigor, and his words were particularly strong. Only the chieftain Badak remained cold and made war-weary remarks. Baso coveted the concubine's beauty and had ulterior motives.

Initially, the Qing army suffered defeats in the conquest of Xinjiang. One day, they suddenly sent an envoy to negotiate peace. Burhanuddin was indecisive and decided to summon Khoja and other chieftains for a meeting. Khoja, having received instructions from the Fragrant Concubine, believed that peace talks meant surrender. He delivered a passionate speech, advocating war. Badak strongly dissented, and Khoja vehemently denounced him. The Qing envoy reiterated their uncompromising stance, and Khoja killed him, making war unavoidable.

The Qing army, with Badak's betrayal, conquered Xinjiang with unstoppable momentum. On the eve of Khoja's departure for battle, the concubine sang and danced to bid him farewell. Unexpectedly, the Qing army launched a surprise night attack. Khoja and others hastily responded, but Badak had already set an ambush with crossbows, and Khoja was killed in battle. Badak then entered the palace to see the concubine, falsely claiming that peace could be negotiated only if the concubine went to Beijing as a hostage, otherwise, the city would be massacred. The concubine agreed.

Emperor Gaozong's conquest of Xinjiang was partly due to the Fragrant Concubine. Upon hearing of the Qing envoy's triumphant return and the capture of the concubine, he was overjoyed. He went to the Western Garden to visit her. At first sight of her beauty, he was enchanted. The sycophantic minister Heshen, anticipating the Emperor's wishes, tried to persuade the concubine, but she suddenly understood and fiercely rebuked him. The Emperor retreated in embarrassment, but his love for the concubine grew stronger.

After entering Beijing, the concubine never stopped longing for her homeland. Heshen requested the Emperor's permission to build a Xinjiang city in the Western Garden to comfort the concubine. The concubine was overjoyed upon seeing the city. She rushed downstairs, and the Xinjiang people in the city bowed to her as before. The concubine almost thought she was dreaming. She eagerly inquired about the situation in her homeland. The people all told lies, except for the old melon seller, who directly accused the concubine of betraying her country. The concubine dejectedly returned, and Emperor Gaozong, hiding behind the curtain, came out and threatened her. The concubine was furious and drew a knife to attack him, but the Emperor narrowly escaped.

The Empress, upon hearing that the Emperor had taken a Xinjiang concubine, became very jealous and complained to the Empress Dowager, strongly arguing that the woman should not be kept. The Empress Dowager had also heard of the concubine's beauty and summoned her. After learning the truth, the Empress Dowager deeply respected and loved her. She advised the Emperor to send her back, but the Emperor firmly refused. The concubine was furious and rebuked Emperor Gaozong, then drew a knife to stab him. The Emperor dodged, but the concubine failed to catch him. At this time, chaos broke out in the palace, and the concubine was finally captured by soldiers.

The Empress Dowager sighed and said, "This woman would rather die than be dishonored. We should help her achieve her integrity." She ordered a white silk to be prepared to grant her death. The concubine was overjoyed at the prospect of death and slowly ascended the platform for hanging. The Emperor could not help but shed tears of sorrow and regret.

Arts

Street Willows, Wall Flowers (Part 2) 125

— Xiaotian

A Treatise on Marital Harmony Worthy of Your Consideration

It's been too much idle talk; now, we should discuss the scope of street willows and wall flowers and the reasons for their existence. Street willows and wall flowers are merely metaphors for being easily accessible, allowing anyone to pluck them. Prostitutes go without saying. When it comes to figures in the entertainment industry, almost nine out of ten dancers are such, and almost half of storytellers, ballad singers, and acrobats are too. We often see this in local news, but most are deceived by their bosses or colleagues. Perhaps due to proximity, female opera singers, film stars, and theater actresses seem to be better off, but one can't say they are entirely exempt. In short, whether they use their beauty to seduce others or are seduced by others, any improper relationship or action outside the realm of art counts. Originally, "street willow, wall flower" wasn't necessarily a bad term, just a distinction between a family flower and a wild flower.

In terms of gender equality, street willows and wall flowers shouldn't exist at all. However, this problem has continuously occurred for thousands of years, both in China and abroad. We can't help but speculate about the reasons for this. According to the principles of transaction, there must be one party willing to sell and one party willing to buy, and the price is not necessarily money for the transaction to take place. A union between a man and a woman naturally requires mutual consent. Logically, if there's mutual consent, they should get engaged and married. Why resort to illicit affairs? If, after marriage, both parties suddenly feel incompatible, they should divorce and seek a new partner, which is the right thing to do. In this sense, the reason why street willows and wall flowers exist can be said to be because the women themselves are willing. The reason they are willing is either because they are forced by livelihood or because the price of their labor isn't as high as the sacrifice of their beauty. Or, they feel that sacrificing their beauty is more enjoyable than the hardships of work. The most pitiful situation is when, if they don't sacrifice their beauty, their work will be oppressed, and they will have no hope of success. To eliminate these things, we can only improve women's education and work efficiency. But this only pertains to the selling side. If there is only selling and no buying, street willows and wall flowers simply cannot exist. Why don't unmarried men seek their true partners? Why do married husbands still go out seeking pleasure when they have wives at home? A superficial solution is to have happy and fulfilling families that make them feel that wasting money and energy outside is not worth it. The fundamental solution is still to improve women's education and work efficiency. We must understand that taking away men's work means taking away men's pay, and taking away men's obligations means taking away men's rights. When the weight on both sides of the scale is equal, whichever side loses weight will tip to the other side, and that side will suffer. As the proverb says, "After getting Long, one desires Shu." If getting Shu means losing Long, I think people wouldn't dare to desire Shu.

It has mobilized all the actors, male and female, from Guohua Film Company. It is predicted that it will cause a huge sensation at that time.

Recent Photo of Wang Huichan 127

Wang Huichan Hired by Carlton 128

— Jiu Geng

Carlton's invitation to the Kylin Child, Wang Huichan, to play the female role has been confirmed. She is scheduled to take the stage on the first of next month. Currently, due to the costumes not yet being completed, there is talk of a delay. Among the people in the performing arts and ticket-selling circles in Shanghai, few know her name. I will briefly describe her background to inform readers. Huichan, also known as Guizhen, is only twenty-nine years old, from the bank of the Yanxi River in Zhejiang. Her ancestor was a famous official in the Qing Dynasty, famous in his hometown. He lived near West Lake, where Huichan was born, so people generally consider her to be from Hangzhou. Her father, Wang Yiquan, is the famous Shanghai qin master, Mr. Wang Baishui. With a family heritage of learning, she is proficient in many plays, and her appearance is graceful and intelligent. Her demeanor is elegant and has the style of a great family. She usually prefers light makeup and has no current bad habits, which is especially commendable. In the past, she has performed as a guest in charity plays, displaying amazing talent and beauty, always earning praise from the audience and being praised as a rising star. The martyr Zhu Xinggong, who sacrificed himself for righteousness, also greatly appreciated her and wrote a poem to praise her: "Rare to combine outstanding talent and jade-like appearance, taking the stage and captivating the audience; after all, her family heritage is evident, indeed reaching mastery; scrutinizing the plot meticulously, humming new tunes clearly; I am also Zhou Lang, able to appreciate music, daring to say my old eyes can still see clearly." (Previously published: January 6 of the eighteenth year in this publication). Zhu rarely praised actors and actresses, never wasting his ink, but he had a unique vision for Huichan, offering much praise and encouragement. Huichan can be proud of herself among her peers.
